<div id="review_1501711685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1501711685" />
    <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc"><img alt="RJ from the LBC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605827139p2/131730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1501711685?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RJ from the LBC" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc">RJ from the LBC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/6989932-the-vampire-lestat">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1501711685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13929800021815651174">The sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_' title='Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Interview with the Vampire</a> focuses on Lestat, probably the most interesting character in the prior book and the central character in many, many more books to come. The story is fascinating when it intertwines with various historical events and places and times, but much less readable during long exasperating periods of existential fretting and romantic yearning. Rice's gothic prose is beautiful at times, overwhelming at others, best in small doses. </span>
  <span id="freeText13929800021815651174" style="display:none">The sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_" title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Interview with the Vampire</a> focuses on Lestat, probably the most interesting character in the prior book and the central character in many, many more books to come. The story is fascinating when it intertwines with various historical events and places and times, but much less readable during long exasperating periods of existential fretting and romantic yearning. Rice's gothic prose is beautiful at times, overwhelming at others, best in small doses. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13929800021815651174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Erika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5666413-erika"><img alt="Erika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361128945p2/5666413.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224271975?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika" href="/user/show/5666413-erika">Erika</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=series-following">series-following</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5666413-erika?shelf=adult">adult</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer224271975" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13850034138541474447"><i>
  <b>Oh Lestat de Lioncourt, how can you be this rebel, <br/>how dare you create such trouble while not giving a single thought to your actions.</b>
</i><br/><br/>This is the second book on The Vampire Chronicles, and it is time for Lestat to tell his story. It starts in the year 1984 if my mind is not playing tricks on me, <br/><br/><i>(wow, i just realized that i was reading this book at the same time with the book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984' title='1984 by George Orwell' rel='nofollow noopener'>1984</a>. Isn't that weird? book set in 1984 while i was reading 1984... no?... but... are you sure?... not even a little</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13850034138541474447" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Oh Lestat de Lioncourt, how can you be this rebel, <br />how dare you create such trouble while not giving a single thought to your actions.</b>
</i><br /><br />This is the second book on The Vampire Chronicles, and it is time for Lestat to tell his story. It starts in the year 1984 if my mind is not playing tricks on me, <br /><br /><i>(wow, i just realized that i was reading this book at the same time with the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984" title="1984 by George Orwell" rel="nofollow noopener">1984</a>. Isn't that weird? book set in 1984 while i was reading 1984... no?... but... are you sure?... not even a little?... well i... whatever, i think it's interesting :P)</i><br /> <br />and Lestat has become a rockstar in a band called precisely <i>"The Vampire Lestat"</i>. This idea of a vampire becoming a rockstar seems a bit ridiculous to me at the beginning because during all the time in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_" title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Interview with the Vampire</a> they were saying Lestat was very handsome and crazy, so to define him later as an actual rockstar seemed a bit of a tool to trick people into thinking he's way cooler than he actually is, it didn't seem like a good idea to me.<br /><br />I couldn't help but imagine him on stage playing guitar and being stalked by millions of fans while, in his nature, he's supposed to be killing to feed, not just being cool and famous and... rockstar... (at this point it wouldn't have surprise me if he started to "sparkle" :S) And he actually sings, he goes onstage and starts singing things like <i>"I'm a vampire, and I'll suck your blood"</i> and other things.<br /><br />So I didn't like that, but luckily this didn't appear much in the book because for almost the entirety of the book Lestat was writing his story. Basically after the interview with Louis, the boy interviewer published the interview as a book which became a best seller, but everybody thought it was a work of fiction not a real thing. <br /><br />Lestat came across this book when he met the guys of the band and wanted to join them, he went to them and told them he was Lestat and got very surprised to realize that they already knew his name. They thought it was really awesome that he came to them and told them he was Lestat from the book interview instead of other famous vampires like Dracula for example. So He read greedily the book and thought he needed to tell his own story, so he typed it all from the beginning when he was turned into one of the damned creatures.<br /><br />His story was really interesting, it covered way too many details of many things, hence the book is long. I really liked especially when other vampires told him a bit of their back story, more specifically Marius. <br /><br />Marius is a very old vampire, he is the vampire who created Armand, and his story is so damn interesting, i wish i could read more about him. Since he is a very old vampire, his beginnings come from a very old age and you see historical facts here of ancient history, it's really fantastic!! All the chapters about Marius are my favorite parts of the book. <br /><br />In this part he also covered the way vampires started to exist in this world, Marius was not one of the first vampires but he sure knows which 2 were the first ones to appear and they are called The Father and The Mother. <b>Oh, i so enjoyed this part of the story, the whole book was worth it just for this part!</b><br /><br />I also like so much all the philosophy it contains about death, life, existence, love, immortality, etc. Anne Rice is a great author, her prose is gorgeous, the descriptions are beautiful, but i can't bring myself to really love her books, sometimes i feel like they drag way too much and i feel the pace so slow and that makes me stop enjoying the story for a greater part of the book.<br /><br />At the ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lestat gets in trouble because he published that book revealing all the secrets of the vampires, names, locations, everything and he's there being a rockstar, exposed to the world without keeping any secrets nor respecting vampire rules. And he's brought great danger over himself and those he loves.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and that leaves you in a sort of cliffhanger. SOOOO, we're in for great adventure for the next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned__The_Vampire_Chronicles___3_" title="The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of the Damned</a>, apparently.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2263168875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263168875" />
    <a title="Kim M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2389794-kim-m"><img alt="Kim M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525186067p2/2389794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263168875?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim M" href="/user/show/2389794-kim-m">Kim M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2389794-kim-m?shelf=lgbtqia-rep">lgbtqia-rep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263168875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8772892792637225415">After reading <i>Interview with the Vampire</i>, Lestat decides that he wants to tell his own story in the form of a book, <i>The Vampire Lestat</i>. He starts his narrative with pre-vampire life, discusses his transformation, and then the bulk of the story describes everything that happened to Lestat pre-Louis.<br/><br/>I loved <i>Interview with the Vampire</i>. If I had read <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> first, I probably would have loved it just as much. Anne Rice's vampires are what vampires should be: dangerous creatures of the nig</span>
  <span id="freeText8772892792637225415" style="display:none">After reading <i>Interview with the Vampire</i>, Lestat decides that he wants to tell his own story in the form of a book, <i>The Vampire Lestat</i>. He starts his narrative with pre-vampire life, discusses his transformation, and then the bulk of the story describes everything that happened to Lestat pre-Louis.<br /><br />I loved <i>Interview with the Vampire</i>. If I had read <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> first, I probably would have loved it just as much. Anne Rice's vampires are what vampires should be: dangerous creatures of the night who prey on humans. However, her vampires are not pure demons--they have bright minds and souls. They can feel remorse, guilt, and love. This humanity adds <b>extra depth</b> to their characters, which adds an <b>extra element of conflict</b> as their monstrous nature seeks to coexist with their desire to not be merely evil and to mean something in the world. And on top of this, Rice is fantastic at making you invested in each of her morally ambiguous characters and in the relationships they form (or don't form) with each other.<br /><br />That being said, I think that Rice's storytelling technique is just okay. At least in the two books I've read, it's very "telly" with relatively few fleshed-out scenes. I didn't mind so much in <i>Interview with the Vampire</i>, since it was just the one book and Louis was literally telling his story in an interview. But when <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> started with the same sort of feel, I almost quit reading because I wasn't sure I could handle another long novel written in the same form. <b>It felt like I was just starting the first book over again</b> with the exact same style of (very long) exposition, and a very similar (at least at the beginning) journey.<br /><br />However, my biggest problem with <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> is Lestat's change of character. When I first started reading, I thought, wait a second, is this supposed to be Lestat? Because it sounds a lot like Louis… And then the rest of the novel proved to be about someone completely different from the Lestat I'd come to know in <i>Interview with the Vampire</i>. I liked Lestat #2, <b>but I could not reconcile him with Lestat #1</b>. I know, I know, there's a section in the epilogue called "Interview with the Vampire" in which Rice acknowledges the contradictions and seeks to explain them away one by one, but honestly, to me that just makes it worse. Because here's the thing. Independently, I like Lestat #2 and the book he's in. But I also liked Lestat #1 and the book he was in. By inventing arbitrary excuses to explain away Lestat #1's behavior, <b>Rice completely invalidates <i>Interview with the Vampire</i></b>. I mean, it isn't inherently wrong for Louis to have a completely inaccurate impression of Lestat that gets cleared up in the second book, but Rice's explanations for Lestat #1's behavior felt too contrived. It felt as though Rice wrote the first book and then later decided to write a second book that would focus on Lestat, but that she wanted Lestat to be more of a sympathetic hero, so she scrambled to invent excuses for all of his misbehavior from the first book. I don't know if that's how it happened, but that's how it felt to me.<br /><br />So basically, if I had read this book independently, I probably would have given it 4 or 5 stars, but since it came after <i>Interview with the Vampire</i> and copied the narrative structure and completely changed Lestat's character, I can only give it three.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8772892792637225415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1114186762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114186762" />
    <a title="Miquel Reina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34207574-miquel-reina"><img alt="Miquel Reina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513490698p2/34207574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114186762?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miquel Reina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miquel Reina" href="/user/show/34207574-miquel-reina">Miquel Reina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=mistery">mistery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=fantasy-yourng-adult">fantasy-yourng-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34207574-miquel-reina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114186762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5365675478693123923">Anne Rice is definitely one of my favorite authors but as I said in my review for "Interview with the Vampire", in my opinion, Vampire Chronicles saga is divided into two parts; Interview with the Vampire and the rest of the books, especially by the shift in their point of view: the first point of view lies on Louis while in second lies on Lestat. That makes the "Vampire Lestat" and subsequent novels a more passionate and less melancholic mood than Interview with the vampire. Rice plunges us int</span>
  <span id="freeText5365675478693123923" style="display:none">Anne Rice is definitely one of my favorite authors but as I said in my review for "Interview with the Vampire", in my opinion, Vampire Chronicles saga is divided into two parts; Interview with the Vampire and the rest of the books, especially by the shift in their point of view: the first point of view lies on Louis while in second lies on Lestat. That makes the "Vampire Lestat" and subsequent novels a more passionate and less melancholic mood than Interview with the vampire. Rice plunges us into the world where light and darkness fight constantly between what's good or evil, what's ethical or unethical. It's a great novel, much more exciting than "Interview with the Vampire" and is ideal for all those fans of the vampire myth and good writing.<br /><br />Spanish version: <br />Anne Rice es sin duda una de mis autoras favoritas pero como ya dije mi crítica para "Entrevista con el Vampiro", en mi opinión la saga de crónicas vampíricas se divide en dos partes; entrevista con el vampiro y el resto de libros, sobre todo por el evidente cambio en el punto de vista, en la primera el punto de vista recae en Louis mientras que en la segunda en Lestat. Eso hace que a Lestat el vampiro y las siguientes novelas tengan un tinte algo más apasionado y mucho menos melancolico. Rice nos sumerge en un mundo en el que la luz y la oscuridad luchan constantemente en un discurso entre el bien y el mal, lo ético y lo perverso. Es una novela genial, mucho más trepidante que "entrevista con el vampiro" y es ideal para todos aquellos fans del mito y de la buena escritura. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5365675478693123923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1464735075974768905"> <b>Vampires are real and Anne Rice is their historian!</b><br/>Anne Rice has created a very detailed world for the vampires that inhabit her world and the vampires in it.   <span id="freeText1464735075974768905" style="display:none"> <b>Vampires are real and Anne Rice is their historian!</b><br />Anne Rice has created a very detailed world for the vampires that inhabit her world and the vampires in it. The first one of her Vampire Chronicles was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_" title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Interview with the Vampire</a> This is the second one.<br />Lestat was born into a noble family in Auvergne, France, a few decades before the French Revolution was to destroy French nobility. He travels to Paris with his friend, Nicholas, to seek their fortunes but it's there that fate in the shape of the vampire, Magnus, finds him. He will no longer know mortality.<br />I have always been attracted to vampires whether it be books, movies, or even TV series such as Buffy, the Vampire Slayer. I remember my daughters loving the Bunnicula series of books which were about a vampire bunny who sucked the juice out of vegetables, with titles like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/183436.The_Celery_Stalks_at_Midnight__Bunnicula___3_" title="The Celery Stalks at Midnight (Bunnicula, #3) by James Howe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Celery Stalks at Midnight</a><br />I plan on continuing The Vampire Chronicles by Anne Rice. I would recommend this series to anyone who is intrigued by vampires.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3305680792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3305680792" />
    <a title="Eric Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen"><img alt="Eric Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560117879p2/6229358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3305680792?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Allen" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen">Eric Allen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3305680792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer328854170231422825">So my GF didn't believe me that there was ever a movie sequel to Interview with a Vampire. So, I dusted off my *cough* VHS tape of if. Wandered around the house swearing I still had a VCR around here somewhere for about an hour. Found that and dusted it off too, and popped the movie in. Wow. that movie. It's sooooooo bad. But it left me wanting to reread this book, and the book after it. I first read these books way back in the beforetimes of 1993 when I was in middle school, and it was just as </span>
  <span id="freeText328854170231422825" style="display:none">So my GF didn't believe me that there was ever a movie sequel to Interview with a Vampire. So, I dusted off my *cough* VHS tape of if. Wandered around the house swearing I still had a VCR around here somewhere for about an hour. Found that and dusted it off too, and popped the movie in. Wow. that movie. It's sooooooo bad. But it left me wanting to reread this book, and the book after it. I first read these books way back in the beforetimes of 1993 when I was in middle school, and it was just as cool to be carrying around an Anne Rice book as it was to be carrying around a Stephen King book. Uh, cool for girls anyway. I got made fun of within an inch of my life for it. But, you know what? I remember really liking this book. It took the villain of the first book, made him kind of a lovable douchebag, and turned the events of the first book on their head, leaving you to decide which of the two narrators was more reliable. Personally, I always thought Lestat was, because he's just a way better character with a way better story than Louis ever was. So, here I am, reading it again, and seeing if the book is as good as I remember it being, or not so much.<br /><br /><br />Okay, I'm 25% done now and I have a couple things to talk about:<br /><br />First, I haven't read an Anne Rice book in 20 some-odd years, so I didn't remember her style of writing very well. She tends to go off on tangents quite a bit, and she has a habit of overdescribing things that are not exactly relevant to the story or characters. I think maybe a bit more of a forceful editor could have straightened this out a bit. It's not really terrible, but it can be annoying when she just randomly changes topics out of nowhere, and then gives like 2 pages of details about some building or person that Lestat happens to glance at and then never visits or sees again. Just, like, FOCUS author, FOCUS ON WHAT'S IMPORTANT. That's all I ask.<br /><br />And second, this is something I didn't really pick up on as a sheltered little Mormon boy back in the '90s, but there are some really interesting ideas about gender and sexuality in this book. Rice explores sexuality through beings that have no need or desire for sex, and for whom gender is basically meaningless. It's an interesting concept that has a lot to say about humanity and gender roles, without actually saying any of it, instead making you think about it yourself. Lestat is unabashedly bisexual, and his mother Gabrielle is transgender, and both of them tend to be a bit gender fluid at times. And, you know, as a 40-something heterosexual dude, to me it seems like it's really well done, like REALLY well done, and woven extremely well into the story. There's never a point where any character sits back and starts explaining his/her/other sexuality and gender identity to us, and what it means. They just are who and what they are, and there's no need to explain, because it's obvious from who and what they are. One of my biggest problems with a recent book called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2737501112" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Name of All Things by Jenn Lyons</a> was that one of the characters was transgender, and this character, just out of nowhere, changes the subject of a conversation that had nothing to do with gender or sexuality, and begins explaining that she is transgender, and what, exactly, that means. And the author just lectures, and lectures, and lectures about it. I know that Jenn Lyons will never read this, but if, by some miracle, she does, PLEASE read The Vampire Lestat and fucking learn how it's supposed to be done!!!! <br /><br />So yeah, despite a few annoyances in the writing style, I'm enjoying this book a lot more than I was expecting to, and it's mostly because of Lestat being a lovable douchebag, and the way the author is handling her characters' sexuality and gender identities, which is pretty amazing for a book that came out in 1985. Here we are 35 years later, and most authors still can't hold a candle to what Anne Rice has done here.<br /><br /><br />70% through:<br /><br />So, from about the time Lestat Vampirizes his mother until Armand's story, this book is kind of abysmally dull. There's not enough going on to justify how much of the book this section takes up, and it's mostly full of the author going off on irrelevant topics for waaaaaaay tooooooo looooooong. Even the conflict with the Paris Coven is pretty boring, though I did like Lestat's "your beliefs are stupid, and you should all be more like me" speech. But Armand's story brings a new focus for the story. Something for Lestat to fixate on and strive towards. I really like the search for Marius. Lestat traveling the world over, looking for clues, studying old myths, and meeting other vampires in different places. I also really like how Lestat and Gabrielle grow apart through their different philosophies on what vampirism should mean. Once Lestat has a quest, giving the story a purpose and direction, it becomes a lot more enjoyable. Until that point, the story doesn't really have much of a point, or any real focus. It's basically Lestat rambling about his life until he learns of the great old ones, and the mystery of Those Who Must Be Kept, and how much such old and powerful beings could teach him. I also like how depressed Lestat was when learning of the deaths of his brothers and their families in the French Revolution. They are only shown to treat him like crap throughout his life, but it shows a new side of him as a character that he feels for their loss, even though he didn't like them very much. It makes him feel a bit more realistic.<br /><br /><br />85% done:<br /><br />Okay, I LOVE Marius' story. Rice attempted, and mostly succeeded in creating a story that has the weight and feel of an old, and almost forgotten legend about the origin of the vampires, and Those Who Must Be Kept. She also did an extremely good job of making the scene where Lestat first sees them feel extremely creepy. If you're not really on board for the meandering, tangential, and far too overdescribed first half of the book, the last half of this book is kind of amazing.<br /><br /><br />100% done:<br /><br />So, This book spends very little time near the end recapping the first book. And it's not really even much of a recap, so much as Lestat feeling sorry for all of the bad things he did, and indignant at the things Louis said about him that weren't true. Most of the recap is about things that happened around Lestat when Louis was elsewhere. It's kind of a really good way of covering ground that has already been covered, but from a different point of view. And holy crap is Armand a heck of a lot more evil and manipulative than he's ever portrayed in either of the movies.<br /><br />So, the whole rockstar thing. That's kind of really dumb. But at the same time, it is SOOOO Lestat. It is EXACTLY what he would do. He always wants to be the center of attention, the star of the stage, etc, and how better to do that, than to make himself into a rock god? I like how he's trying to break all of the rules and try to show the mortal world that immortals exist. And it's really fitting that hearing his music wakes Akasha and sends her out on her murder spree of vampires. The book ends with a cliffhanger, and iirc the next book doesn't get to what happens next with him until about the halfway point, instead dealing with Maharet, her family, and how Akasha was overthrown back in ancient Egypt.<br /><br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed this book a lot more 25 years after my first reading it that I expected to. It's not without it's flaws, but Lestat is a pretty entertaining character, and the author creates some extremely good mythology around her vampires. There are some pretty good characters, and some great stories from older vampires about their lives. The book also does a really excellent job of exploring sexuality and gender identity without grinding your nose in it like modern authors seem to think they need to do. Definitely a worthy sequel to Interview with the Vampire, as it expands upon what was given in the first book, and builds a bigger, more elaborate world atop its foundation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="328854170231422825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_414455256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414455256" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/753983-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347063809p2/753983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/414455256?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/753983-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/753983-michelle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414455256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12271168874970088167">TL;DR - it's worth reading if you enjoy the franchise, the characters, and are willing to self-edit (that is, skip the repetitive expositions).<br/><br/>Although I read this book when it was first published, and reread it a time or two in the intervening decades, most recently I "read" this book as an audio book, which is an interesting test for a book. The book is in the first person, so listening to it heightens the effect of Lestat telling you his story; however, I hadn't realized how much of the ponti</span>
  <span id="freeText12271168874970088167" style="display:none">TL;DR - it's worth reading if you enjoy the franchise, the characters, and are willing to self-edit (that is, skip the repetitive expositions).<br /><br />Although I read this book when it was first published, and reread it a time or two in the intervening decades, most recently I "read" this book as an audio book, which is an interesting test for a book. The book is in the first person, so listening to it heightens the effect of Lestat telling you his story; however, I hadn't realized how much of the pontificating I usually skipped over when rereading the book in print. At times during the narration I wanted to stop Lestat and tell him, "I get it--you've made your point. Move along, please." I had forgotten the endless exposition about the nature of good and evil and spirituality, and I had forgotten how much Lestat verges on being a "Mary Sue" (an overly idealized character). His flaws are extensive, some of which even acknowledged in faux-self-deprecation, but somehow everyone loves him despite these flaws, and forgives him the most outrageous transgressions, which always end up benefitting him.<br /><br />The character of Gabrielle has always been more interesting to me than Lestat. Where his extreme extraversion annoys me, her uncompromising introversion attracts. Where Lestat's transformation to vampire leads him to endless ruminations about the need to love humans and humanity, his dependence on and need of them, the utter lack of meaning in a life without the love of humans, Gabrielle uses her transformation to free her at last from the demands and needs of others. She sticks around for a few transitional decades to try to wean her son into adult independence, but ultimately puts her own selfhood first. <br /><br />Detaching to look at the structure of the book, the tale within a tale is carried too far, and by the time Lestat meets up with Marius, I was snorting as I counted the layers, as we have Lestat, who tells us the tale of himself listening to Marius, as Marius relates the tale of Marius listening to the tale of the Egyptian priest, who relates the story of Those Who Must Be Kept. There may have been another layer in there, but who can keep track? While the individual embedded stories were interesting, they also felt like a massive info dump, to give us the necessary background to appreciate the amazing specialness of Lestat, when he is the one to whom the Queen (silent and unmoving for centuries) responds.<br /><br />If you're going to read this book for the first time, make sure you have the next book "Queen of the Damned" ready, as "The Vampire Lestat" ends in a cliffhanger. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12271168874970088167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1555891608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1555891608" />
    <a title="Jess The Bookworm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32042916-jess-the-bookworm"><img alt="Jess The Bookworm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454940122p2/32042916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1555891608?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess The Bookworm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess The Bookworm" href="/user/show/32042916-jess-the-bookworm">Jess The Bookworm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32042916-jess-the-bookworm?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555891608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9903674441009943701">This is the sequel to Interview with the Vampire, in which Lestat de Lioncourt awakens in the 1980s, reads Louis' account of the events in Interview with the Vampire, and decides to set the record straight. <br/><br/>Lestat takes us back to his upbringing as the son of a Marquis in France, where even as a mortal, he was in the thoes of an existential crisis, filled with the need to escape his family home. He runs away with his lover to Paris, where they join the theatre. It is here that Lestat is turned, </span>
  <span id="freeText9903674441009943701" style="display:none">This is the sequel to Interview with the Vampire, in which Lestat de Lioncourt awakens in the 1980s, reads Louis' account of the events in Interview with the Vampire, and decides to set the record straight. <br /><br />Lestat takes us back to his upbringing as the son of a Marquis in France, where even as a mortal, he was in the thoes of an existential crisis, filled with the need to escape his family home. He runs away with his lover to Paris, where they join the theatre. It is here that Lestat is turned, and his whole life changes. <br /><br />This is a very philosophical book. Lestat has a lot of feelings, even as a mortal, he cries at the drop of a hat and goes into despair. When he becomes a vampire he is just as emotional. This book takes the reader through his musings on the meaning of life, immortality, love, good and evil. For this reason, I would say that it isn't an easy reading book, and you have to be in the mood to be contemplative. When you are in the mood, it is extremely fascinating.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed the glimpse given into the origin of vampires as a species, and I now cannot wait to read the next book.<br /><br />I am officially hooked on this series, and I already know that I will be re-reading this book in the near future.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9903674441009943701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2uY2D+eTRMokeJTBi9rM+yh9su4v4GmEYbMQmyN/10BTBq07juxblzr50DVlZG3Z1mM+7I/rCwzCieFJ0DbsVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jmr+q17FyNjM4EKOyYjtUR4h6nK8T5y3kYHtsN0aQDsHimWfN7rXhdJhBnonNkxz4D9mcBxE/j8yuxxiLlN7Lg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3474755385220463188">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText3474755385220463188" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>

Louis recounts how he became a vampire at the hands of the radiant and sinister Lestat and how he became indoctrinated, unwillingly, into the vampire way of life. His story ebbs and flows through the streets of New Orleans, defining crucial moments such as his discovery of the exquisite lost young child Claudia, wanting not to hurt but to comfort her with the last breaths of humanity he has inside. Yet, he makes Claudia a vampire, trapping her womanly passion, will, and intelligence inside the body of a small child. Louis and Claudia form a seemingly unbreakable alliance and even &quot;settle down&quot; for a while in the opulent French Quarter. Louis remembers Claudia\'s struggle to understand herself and the hatred they both have for Lestat that sends them halfway across the world to seek others of their kind. Louis and Claudia are desperate to find somewhere they belong, to find others who understand, and someone who knows what and why they are.\n\nLouis and Claudia travel Europe, eventually coming to Paris and the ragingly successful Theatre des Vampires--a theatre of vampires pretending to be mortals pretending to be vampires. Here they meet the magnetic and ethereal Armand, who brings them into a whole society of vampires. But Louis and Claudia find that finding others like themselves provides no easy answers and in fact presents dangers they scarcely imagined.\n\nOriginally begun as a short story, the book took off as Anne wrote it, spinning the tragic and triumphant life experiences of a soul. As well as the struggles of its characters, Interview captures the political and social changes of two continents. The novel also introduces Lestat, Anne\'s most enduring character, a heady mixture of attraction and revulsion. The book, full of lush description, centers on the themes of immortality, change, loss, sexuality, and power.\nsource: annerice.com<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13882728613748227039\" href=\"#\" in a feat of mesmeric storytelling, a chillingly hypnotic entertainment in which the oldest and most powerful forces of the night are unleashed on an unsuspecting world.Three brilliantly colored narrative threads intertwine as the story unfolds:- The rock star known as Vampire Lestat, worshipped by millions of spellbound fans, prepares for a concert in San Francisco.  Among the audience--pilgrims in a blind swoon of adoration--are hundreds of vampires, creatures who see Lestat as a &quot;greedy fiend risking the secret prosperity of all his kind just to be loved and seen by mortals,&quot; fiends themselves who hate Lestat\'s power and who are determined to destroy him . . . - The sleep of certain men and women--vampires and mortals scattered around the world--is haunted by a vivid, mysterious dream: of twins with fiery red hair and piercing green eyes who suffer an unspeakable tragedy.  It is a dream that slowly, tauntingly reveals its meaning to the dreamers as they make their way toward each other--some to be destroyed on the journey, some to face an even more terrifying fate at journey\'s end . . . - Akasha--Queen of the Damned, mother of all vampires, rises after a 6,000 year sleep and puts into motion a heinous plan to &quot;save&quot; mankind from itself and make &quot;all myths of the world real&quot; by elevating herself and her chosen son/lover to the level of the gods: &quot;I am the fulfillment and I shall from this moment be the cause&quot; . . . These narrative threads wind sinuously across a vast, richly detailed tapestry of the violent, sensual world of vampirism, taking us back 6,000 years to its beginnings.  As the stories of the &quot;first brood&quot; of blood drinkers are revealed, we are swept across the ages, from Egypt to South America to the Himalayas to all the shrouded corners of the globe where vampires have left their mark. Vampires are created--mortals succumbing to the sensation of &quot;being enptied, of being devoured, of being nothing.&quot; Vampires are destroyed.  Dark rituals are performed--the rituals of ancient creatures prowling the modern world.  And, finally, we are brought to a moment in the twentieth century when, in an astonishing climax, the fate of the living dead--and perhaps of the living, all the
